Labor Dispute Over Layoffs at Feixing Rickshaw Company 143

Party and Government Agencies Failed to Mediate Yesterday Morning

The Feixing Rickshaw Company on Baoshan Road, Zhabei, employs a total of 159 workers. Recently, manager Gu Songmao informed the workers that the shareholders were planning to dissolve the company and wanted to downsize. On the 20th, the lamp repair department was closed, and the workers in that department would be dismissed next month. At the same time, it was proposed to reduce the number of workers in the shop department, hiring only 70% of the carpenters, blacksmiths, ironworkers, tailors, and painters. This has sparked opposition from all the workers. According to the workers, they were hired by the former manager, a Westerner named Guoren. Since Gu took over in the 16th year, it seems he is just using the Feixing brand, and it is unknown whether the Westerner actually sold the company to Gu. Logically speaking, Gu has no right to make changes. However, the management stated that they acquired the company from the Westerner in the 16th year for a fixed term of five and a half years, which has now expired, and the foreign company should continue to operate the company. The workers had no choice but to petition party and government agencies for mediation. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, party and government agencies summoned representatives from both labor and management to the Social Affairs Bureau for mediation. The labor representatives were Jing Shengyu and Xu Fuji, and the management representatives were Gu Songmao and Bao Bing. Dai Yongchan of the Municipal Party Headquarters and Zhu Jintao of the Social Affairs Bureau chaired the meeting. In the end, the management refused to reinstate the workers in the closed department and insisted on maintaining the status quo, resulting in failed mediation. The party and government representatives then ordered both parties to leave and try to reach an agreement on their own. If no agreement is reached, another mediation session will be scheduled.

The Fourth District Branch of the Nanyang Overseas Chinese Association of the French Concession of this port and the Shanghai Second Special District Citizens Federation sent a letter to the General Association yesterday regarding the French Municipal Council's collection of awning tax, requesting negotiations to stop it. The original letter is transcribed below: "To whom it may concern, we have received complaints from member businesses such as the Dayouxing Wine Store and Deyuan Restaurant in the Bailuer Road area, stating that due to the recent hot weather, they have put up cloth awnings in front of their stores to provide shade. However, they have been repeatedly notified by the police to pay taxes and have been arbitrarily fined. Our awnings are not suspended in the air, but only hung from the front of the building and are very high off the ground. We cannot accept this unreasonable and harsh tax. We request that your association negotiate and stop this tax, and prevent the police from issuing fines." "Shops hang cloth awnings to block the sun, which not only does not obstruct traffic but also benefits pedestrians. Moreover, the awnings are only hung for three months. To levy a large amount of taxes in such a short period of time is truly a harsh tax that disturbs the people. Your association has repeatedly negotiated with the French authorities, and the authorities have agreed to submit the matter to the Board of Directors for discussion. However, according to reports from various shops, the collection of taxes continues as before, and the police are using intimidation and punishment, which is completely unreasonable and disruptive. We are writing to request that your association promptly negotiate with the French authorities and stop the imposition of penalties until the matter is resolved, so as to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. We await your urgent instructions."

All Employees in the Used Clothing Industry to Stop Shouting While Eating 145

Lianyi Society Sets to Implement it Starting July 1

Employees in the used clothing industry were outraged that employers were still making them shout while eating, leaving them no time to rest after a full meal, which was detrimental to their health. Considering the national crisis, they prudently submitted a request to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the General Labor Union to uphold the existing conditions, instructing the Used Clothing Industry Association to relay to all employers to comply with the original conditions to prevent unexpected disputes. On the other hand, they will implement a complete cessation of shouting while eating starting July 1 to emphasize humanitarianism.

Over 600 Refugees from Jiangxi Arrive in Shanghai 146

Rations Issued by Name

Plans to Send Them Back to Their Hometown Soon

Due to natural disasters and man-made calamities in various areas of Ruijin County, Jiangxi, the people have no clothes or food and cannot live in peace. Three years ago, gentry members Liu Shengpeng and Yang Shiying, along with Yang Rongliu and other members of the Public Security Bureau and the Local Autonomy Preparatory Office, led over 700 refugees, begging along the way, and fleeing to Guangdong. After receiving passports issued by the county head of Jiaoling County, Guangdong Province, 130 people arrived in Shanghai on the Zhaoshangju's Fair Wheel. Another 491 people arrived in Shanghai on the Taikoo Company's Xinjiang Wheel, totaling over 600 people. They arrived in Shanghai on the afternoon of the day before yesterday and disembarked at the Zhaoshangju New Pier in Nanshi. Afterwards, Sun Yulin, a patrol officer from the First Precinct of the Pudong Third District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Wu Zuojing, a policeman from the First Division of the First District, went to maintain order and temporarily housed them in the Jiangxi Guild Hall at Xiaoputuo Bridge outside Xiaonanmen. Yesterday morning, representatives of the refugees went to the Social Affairs Bureau to register and to the Public Security Bureau to request relief. Hong Qiwen, the chief of the Second Section, sent Yin Guanzhi, the director of the relief division, to issue rations by name. Plans are being made to send them to Nanchang, Jiangxi, for further processing.

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry to Inspect Exported Poultry Feathers 147

|Implementation Upon Approval by the Ministry|

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry has recently found that the export of poultry feathers from China is significant. However, ordinary merchants are unaware of the customs inspection standards of various countries. Sometimes, exports are rejected for not meeting hygiene standards and are forced to return, resulting in significant losses. Recognizing this, the bureau is now inspecting exported feathers according to the Commodity Inspection Regulations. A report has been submitted to the Ministry, and once approved, merchants will be notified to send all exported feathers to the bureau for inspection before export. If the feathers are deemed qualified, it can be guaranteed that they will be allowed to be imported into any foreign country, avoiding unnecessary trips and hardship for merchants.

###徵國產綢緞展覽會

The Chinese National Silk and Satin Exhibition, initiated by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce based on the proposal of the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank and Silk and Satin Industry Groups, is now underway. Details are as follows:

Seeking Exhibits 148

The association issued a call for submissions yesterday, stating, "For many years, domestic silk and satin have suffered from the dumping of imported goods, resulting in declining business, making people's livelihoods increasingly difficult, and the national economy more and more strained. In order to rescue the industry and promote domestic goods, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce decided at a joint supervisory committee meeting on June 24th to establish the Chinese National Silk and Satin Exhibition, jointly organized by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the National Goods Market, the Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association, the Shanghai Electrical Machinery Silk Weaving Industry Association, and the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank. The entire third floor of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Commodity Exhibition Hall will be used as the exhibition venue. Preparations are actively underway, and the opening is scheduled for July 9th. We sincerely hope that all factories in the silk and satin industry, both locally and abroad, will quickly prepare new and innovative exhibits and submit them to the Chinese National Silk and Satin Exhibition Exhibit Collection Office located within the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce before July 6th, so that we can arrange the displays and open on schedule for public viewing, allowing the public to recognize the value of domestic brocade and the agricultural and silkworm industries can be revitalized. The national economy and people's livelihoods will be greatly benefited. In addition to sending separate letters, we hereby issue this notice."

Jisheng Society's Record of Well Drilling and Irrigation in Wugong, Shaanxi 152

This year, the Chinese Jisheng Society in this port has spent funds on emergency relief and seed distribution in Wugong, Shaanxi. Mr. Wang, a philanthropist, is deeply concerned about the frequent droughts in the counties of Shaanxi, especially the severe disaster in Wugong, which has left the people in dire straits. The dry fields lack ponds and weirs, and the crops cannot be irrigated, making it difficult to predict the harvest. In light of this, Mr. Wang donated 1,000 yuan to the society to test the drilling of five wells in the rural areas of the county. The Society has sent letters to the Chang'an Branch and the gentry of Wugong County, requesting them to send personnel to investigate suitable locations, assess the depth and width of the wells, and create designs for the construction of the millstone well railings, and to send diagrams and explanations to the Society for review and approval before construction commences. This will enable water conservation and benefit agricultural land. If any philanthropist can continue to provide funds for drilling, it would be a great act of merit to promote water conservation and universally help all living beings.

Zhabei Public Bus Extends Shanghai-Jiangwan Service Hours 153

|Starting July 1st|

Since resuming operations after the war, the Shanghai Huashang Public Bus Company, which operates the Jiangwan-Shanghai line, has been gradually extending its service hours. The last bus was initially extended from 6:00 PM to 8:00 PM. Now that summer is here, and the days are longer, the company will extend its last bus again, starting July 1st, to facilitate travel. After 8:00 PM, a bus will depart every 30 minutes. The last bus from Shanghai to Jiangwan will depart at 9:30 PM, and the last bus from Jiangwan to Shanghai will depart at 10:00 PM.

Record of the Success of the Harmonica Concert 155

The China Harmonica Society held its second anniversary concert at the Yingshi Memorial Hall of the Lake Society on the evenings of the 23rd and 24th of this month. Around 1,500 people attended. Directors and advisors of the society, such as Gu Yu, Pan Yangyao, Huang Jinwu, Yang Linzhi, Xing Dingcheng, Xu Weigong, Huang Jingwan, and others, as well as reporters from Chinese and Western newspapers, and people from Britain and Germany, numbered no less than 100. Each evening, the concert began at 8:00 PM. Society President and Director Wang Qingxun gave an opening speech. The music then began. In the first section, the society's harmonica team, consisting of over 50 men and women, performed a large ensemble of the Party Song and the overture to "Heaven and Hell." This was followed by a performance of "Elegy in Memory of Fallen Soldiers" and "Black Horse Galloping," which were highly praised. The song "Nineteenth Route Army March," composed by Wang himself, was particularly well-received. The song was passionate and inspiring, symbolizing the Nineteenth Route Army soldiers charging into battle. The audience was deeply moved. Mr. Yang, the director of the recording department of the Shanghai Victory Company, felt that Wang's song was tragic and passionate and would inspire the patriotism of the people, and has specially invited the society's harmonica team to record the harmonica song for the company. In the second section, Kunqu opera "Amitabha Buddha," famous opera "La Traviata," "Carmen," and "Invitation to the Dancing Party" were performed. The "Amitabha Buddha" was performed with wooden fish and chanting, which was quite interesting. When listening with eyes closed, it was as if one were in the temple. "La Traviata" and "Carmen" are Spanish-style dance tunes, which are melodious. It was as if one were listening to the high mountain flowing water, which made all the one thousand people feel great. "Invitation to the Dancing Party" had a melodious sound, and the tone was excellent, causing people to want to dance. Guests who participated in the performance included Wei Zhongle from the Datong Music Society with his Pipa song "Huaiyin Pingchu" and Guqin, Li Kainan with his Hawaiian marching song on his guitar, the Wu Ping Music Troupe from Wu County with their Chinese music "Lianhuan Kou," and Jiang Shouliang with his Banhu "Chu Huan Xiao Chang." They were all well-received by the audience and performed three songs in a row. Wang, the president of the association, performed a harmonica solo, his famous Cantonese ancient tune "Xiao Tao Hong," which was quiet and subtle, captivating the audience. He also played "Han Gong Qiu Yue," which was also very beautiful and gentle. The concert ended and it was very late.

Shanghai business magnate Mr. Yin Xinzhi, after returning from the political arena, engaged in the construction business and established the Dachang Construction Company. Chinese Martial Arts Circus Arriving in Shanghai from Hong Kong 157

Circuses have always been dominated by foreigners, and Chinese people have never been involved. Now, a large-scale Chinese martial arts circus, composed of Chinese martial arts experts, both male and female, has been performing amazing stunts in major ports in England, France, Holland, Siam, India, and other places for four years, leaving audiences in awe. In Siam, during the "Flying Trapeze" act, the actors performed aerial stunts with great danger, surpassing anything foreign circuses had ever done. The Siamese Emperor awarded them generously and gave them a reward of 800 baht. In Burma, during the performance of the "Double Suspension" act, the Burmese Governor's Office requested a repeat performance. This shows how well-received they are everywhere. Many fine horses, elephants, tigers, lions, leopards, and other animals have been collected from abroad for performances and are well-trained to perform in sequence. There are also various clever stunts, such as "Girl Riding a Horse" and "Elephant Stepping on People." The variety is endless. Now, in response to invitations from all walks of life, they have returned to China. They will make a short stop in Hong Kong and will arrive in Shanghai soon. It is expected that people from all walks of life will want to see them as soon as possible.

The Investigation of the Xin Renhe Massacre Yesterday Involved the Interrogation of Comprador Chen Baosheng 158

Sun Xingsheng and 22 other defendants in the Xin Renhe ship massacre case have been sentenced. Chen Baosheng, the absconding deputy comprador in the verdict, came to Shanghai to visit his sick wife and children and was captured by the detectives of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. He has been transferred to the local court. After a preliminary hearing by Prosecutor Zhang, he was ordered to be detained. Since the case had already been prosecuted, and Chen Baosheng was a fugitive at the time, he was prosecuted in absentia. The Prosecutor's Office sent Chen for trial. Yesterday, Judge Luo opened an investigation court to interrogate Chen Baosheng, who claimed that he was already asleep when the killings occurred and knew nothing about them. Later, Wang Guanxian forced him to sign the document, threatening him with the same treatment if he refused. The judge instructed him that since the case was an investigation, he could appoint a defense lawyer himself, and then the court would reconvene for a debate, and ordered him to be taken back into custody.

Lu Tongcheng Commits Suicide by Poisoning 159

=Received a warning letter from the Anti-Treason Group, embezzled opium, and committed suicide=

Minhua Sen Umbrella Factory, located at No. 661, Jiucang Street intersection, Laobeimen, Minguo Road, was opened by Lu Tongcheng (38 years old) from Jingjiang. Its business was quite prosperous. However, due to the nature of his business, he inevitably purchased enemy goods and raw materials. Therefore, he received a letter previously, which was identified as a warning letter from the Anti-Treason Group. Lu was greatly surprised. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 26th of this month, he received another letter from the Anti-Treason Group, which depicted a bomb, a pistol, and a dagger. The language inside was extremely intense. After reading the letter, Lu immediately turned pale and looked worried. He was restless inside the house, either walking slowly or sitting silently with his head propped up, his brow furrowed with deep concern. When he went out alone in the evening, he returned home at 9 o'clock, lying down on the bed. His family was not yet aware of his situation. Around 10 o'clock, Lu, lying in bed, made a terrible moaning sound. His family went to inquire, and he shook his head in tears, unable to speak. Realizing that he had taken poison, his younger brother, Lu Tongyuan, immediately took him to Renji Hospital for treatment. He was diagnosed with opium poisoning, but because he had ingested a large amount and the time had passed, he could not be saved. He lingered until 6 o'clock yesterday morning when he finally succumbed. His brother then reported the information to the trade association and the First Precinct of the Second District, requesting an investigation. That precinct then ordered Jiang Pingyang, the Jiupu landlord, to report to the District Court for verification in the afternoon. Subsequently, the prosecutor and others arrived at the court and confirmed the cause of death. The brother was instructed to collect the body for burial after proper verification.

Crushed to Death by Streetcar, Death from Heatstroke 160

Jin Yan, a Ningbo woman residing near Gaochang Temple in South Shanghai, usually sold vegetables. Yesterday morning, around 8 o'clock, she was carrying a vegetable basket on her shoulder and taking her four-year-old son, Mao Yin, with her. While passing near Bansongyuan, she was hit and crushed in the head and face by streetcar No. 28 of the Fourth Route of the Huashang Electric Tramway Company, and died instantly. The patrol police arrived and took the driver, Zhao Puzhong (39 years old, from Taixing), to the Second District Police Station. The child's father, Jin Shuangxing, was unemployed at home and was an only child. The woman witnessed her beloved son's tragic death and immediately grabbed the streetcar, wailing loudly and violently hitting her head against the streetcar, intending to die with her son, causing extreme distress.

In front of the Yaoye (pharmacy) Association on Taiping Street in the Hongqiao area of the city, an unidentified male corpse was found yesterday. He was about 40 years old and wearing a black cloth short shirt and trousers. The police ordered Qian Shaoqing, the Jiupu landlord, to report to the District Court for verification. Prosecutor Li and others arrived at the scene and confirmed that he died of heatstroke. The body was placed in a coffin for burial.

Japanese National Drug Offender Lin Kaitai 161

At 9:00 a.m. the other day, Ding Zhaoxu, a guard at the North Railway Station, discovered a Japanese national, Lin Kaitai, of Chinese descent, in possession of opium paste and drug paraphernalia at the station. He was turned over to the Fifth District Police Station along with the evidence. After questioning by Director Jin, the defendant confessed his name was Lin Kaitai, from Xiamen, and had acquired Japanese nationality. He stated he brought the paraphernalia and opium paste for his own use. He also presented a Japanese travel permit for verification. Since the suspect was of Japanese nationality, the Japanese Consulate General was immediately notified and dispatched a police officer, Higuchi Riuzaemon, to the station to take Lin Kaitai for questioning.

Bandit Traces Seen on the Penglai Road 162

Loss of Over 400 Yuan

Li Huaying's home, located at No. 383, Penglai Road, Xiaoximen in the Southern District, was suddenly visited by three bandits around 7:00 p.m. the other night. Each held a pistol and forbade anyone to make a sound. They simultaneously broke into the bedroom, overturning boxes and chests, and looting for half an hour before escaping with their loot. After a detailed investigation, the loss, including clothing and silver dollars, totaled about 400 yuan. The victim then reported the situation to the Second Sub-precinct of the Second District, requesting that the bandits be apprehended.

Young Girl Deceived and Brought to Shanghai for Prostitution 163

=Mother Received News and Tracked Her to Shanghai, Reported to the Police, and Escaped from the Pit of Fire=

Dong Yan, a woman from Hangzhou, made a living washing clothes. She had a daughter named Jin Feng, who was 18 years old and possessed captivating beauty. Because of poverty, she worked as a female worker at the Fangzheng Tea Shop in Hangzhou. Dai Ronglin, a pockmarked man, knew the Dong family. Seeing Jin Feng's beauty, he harbored bad intentions. On the 21st day of the second lunar month of this year, he went to the Fangzheng Tea Shop and deceptively told Jin Feng that there were many factories in Shanghai and that the wages were quite high. He claimed that he had recommended her to work in a silk stocking factory and ordered her to go to Shanghai with him. If she refused, he threatened that something dangerous might happen. Jin Feng was young and lacked knowledge, and she was deceived and intimidated by Dai's tricks. She went to Shanghai with him and stayed at Dai's house at No. 80, Pu Road. Dai then negotiated with a client. When the time came, Dai claimed that he was taking the girl to the hotel to take a bath and led Jin Feng to the hotel where she had sexual relations with the client. Dai received 100 yuan for this. After that, Dai sold Jin Feng to the Geisha house opened by He Faguei from Nanjing at No. 56, Jing'an Lane, Longmen Road, for 30 yuan. From then on, she was trapped in the pit of fire, living a life of prostitution. Every evening, when the sun set and the lights came on, He sent a maid to accompany Jin Feng to various amusement parks to solicit customers (commonly known as "tangbai") and exchanged her body for money, living the life of a goddess. The night income was split between He and Jin Feng. Jin Feng found this life very painful, and worried about her old mother, who was in great distress after her disappearance. She told He Faguei about being deceived by Dai and asked to send a letter to her mother to prepare the money for her redemption. He agreed and sent a letter to Dong Yan in Hangzhou last month. After receiving the letter, she finally learned the location of her daughter and borrowed travel expenses from relatives the other day to take a train to Shanghai, going directly to He's place on Longmen Road. However, He demanded 50 yuan before he would release her daughter. Because she was destitute and had no money, she had no choice but to report to the Xinzha police station. Detective Zhao Qingkui, bao detective Xu Huanqing, and west detective Qijiagsheng were dispatched to bring He Faguei and Dong Jin Feng to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Li Zhishan explained the above situation. He was now prosecuted under Article 258, Section 2 of the Criminal Law. Judge Qian Wenji questioned Dong Yan, Dong Jin Feng, and the defendant He Faguei, and immediately sentenced He to six months in prison with a two-year reprieve for the crime of inducing others to profit. Jin Feng was taken back by her mother, Dong Yan, after making a written guarantee.

Suspicious Bandits on the Shanghai-Minhang Road 164

Letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to Pay Attention

Xiang Liansun, the owner of Hechang Pengxing, located at No. 1099, Peng Road, Broadway, Hongkou, hired bodyguards to accompany him in and out due to the bad social environment. The other day, he went to Minhang on business and hired a car from the Huabei Automobile Company. He went in the afternoon. Unexpectedly, at 2:30 pm, when the car reached the left side of Xujiahui (i.e. Tushanwan), near Zhongshan Road, he saw two men in short clothes in front. As soon as they saw the car, they ran forward quickly. At the corner of the road, the two men stopped, one raised his hand as a signal, and at the same time a man in a suit jumped out from the left, raised his hand and ordered the car to stop. The three men each took out a pistol to threaten him, intending to kidnap him. However, Xiang also had his own pistol and ordered his bodyguards to take out their pistols, aim, and defend themselves. At the same time, he urged the driver to drive quickly, so he was able to escape. It was said that they were bandits or robbers, but they did not succeed. It was said that they were plainclothes detectives investigating criminals, but they did not identify themselves. Judging from their actions, they were definitely not good people, either kidnapping or robbing. At that time, the crisis was imminent. Afterwards, Xiang, considering that the place was the Shanghai-Minhang thoroughfare and there were many Chinese and foreign people coming and going, for the sake of public security, specially sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau yesterday, requesting that the district office be ordered to strictly arrest bandits and take proper precautions.

Child Killed by Streetcar 165

Jin Shuangxi, a Hangzhou native, lived at No. 55, Jiuda Lane, Bansongyuan Road, Nanshi. He married Yan and had a four-year-old son nicknamed Mao Lin. Yesterday morning around 8:00, Yan went out to buy groceries. Her son, Mao Lin, suddenly stumbled alone onto the road to play. In an instant, he rushed into the streetcar tracks. At that time, a streetcar No. 28 of the Fourth Route of the Huashang Electric Tramway Company, speeding from north to south, was approaching. Mao Lin was unable to avoid it, was knocked to the ground, and rolled under the car, suffering serious injuries to his head and arms, and died instantly. The nearby police heard the news and rushed to the scene. They brought Zhao Puzhong, the driver of the fifth car, to the Second District Headquarters. Record of the Executive Committee Meeting of the Medical Association 169

The Shanghai Medical Association held its ninth executive committee meeting yesterday. Xu Naili, Pang Jingzhou, Liu Zhigang, Cai Yumen, Yu Yunxiu, Xie Yunshou, Wu Yichu, Ye Zhisheng, Jin Wenhong, Zhu Yanggao (Yu replaced), Wang Qizhang (Xu replaced), Xia Shenchu (Pang replaced), and Jiang Zhenxun (Pang replaced) attended. Xu Naili chaired the meeting and the following were discussed: (1) The Municipal Health Bureau sent a letter urging all members to uniformly abide by the association's new system of weights and measures (resolved) A letter was sent to the Health Bureau stating that the association mistakenly believed that the new weights and measures system was the municipal system. The association had already notified members to check the new system earlier. News About Charitable Activities in the Pushan Villa 171

Pushan Villa handles the burial of exposed corpses in Shanghai, respecting humanity and emphasizing hygiene. It also provides medical treatment and medicine to relieve the poor and sick, truly seeking happiness for the local people. Since 1928, in accordance with the wishes of Mr. Wang Yiting, the idea was that coffins are not buried in Jiangzhe hinterland, forming a bad habit, the bones are piling up, which is unbearable to see. Therefore, he was entrusted with the task of burying the coffins in the hinterland of Jiangzhe. To date, a total of 71,261 exposed coffins and bones have been collected. The next round of handling will face funding difficulties, and it is feared that it will be suspended. In addition, the river channels in Suzhou City are extremely polluted, and dead animals are often thrown into the river, affecting drinking water hygiene. The dredging work started last year, and as of May of this year, a total of 1,024 dead animals such as cats and dogs and 97 and a half boats of garbage were dredged, all of which were transported to Hengshanbang for burial. In addition, 35 dried public wells were repaired, all of which were used for drinking water by residents, and some repairs were made. Such practical charitable activities and public health have a great relationship. They are all carefully planned by Mr. Wang Junsheng, the director of the villa, and the residents have benefited a lot. However, the villa has no specific funds for charitable activities and relies entirely on donations from all walks of life to maintain it. At this time, it is not easy to raise donations, and regular expenses cannot be reduced. We have to ask for help to increase contributions. We urge kind people from all walks of life to donate generously and participate in charitable activities, so that the villa can continue its various charitable activities. The merits are immeasurable. It is also heard that the comrades of the Leshan Society are enthusiastically supporting the villa and will also hold a theatrical performance to raise funds. It is believed that benefactors from all walks of life will definitely enthusiastically help at that time.

▲Yongsheng Sells Sanitary Rice Yongsheng Rice Shop was established on the Nanhao Road, Laozhagang more than 40 years ago. Its goods have always been genuine and the price has been fair. Recently, with decades of experience, they have found that the season will inevitably be rainy and everything will ferment. Therefore, the human body is also prone to fatigue at this time, due to poor rice quality. In recent years, most of the rice shops in Shanghai have been selling white rice, but there are few sanitary rice on sale. It is not known that machine-milled white rice, although beautiful and palatable, has lost its natural nourishing properties (i.e. vitamins), while the nourishing sanitary rice is not promoted. The shop has come up with a unique idea and set up a factory in the interior, hiring workers to manually clean the white rice and transport it to Shanghai for low-cost sale. Because the rice is truly manually cleaned, the rice quality is exquisite and has a unique fragrance. Eating it can strengthen the spleen and stomach and prevent beriberi.

Reader's Advisor

How to Rescue a Family from Bankruptcy and a Precarious Livelihood? 178

丨 Letter from Zhou Huanzhong of Wucheng, Jiangxi 丨

I am a young man approaching the age of twenty, but I am still young and lack any sense of awareness. My family lives in a small village in Juxin County, Jiangxi. My grandfather and father were both charitable people, just farmers in the village. Because they were financially strapped and had no means of earning a living, they struggled to raise my uncle. When my uncle was sixteen, he was apprenticed to a silk thread shop in Xiushui. After completing his apprenticeship, he opened a small silk thread shop there, and I studied in Xiushui for a few years. The shop's business was quite good, with profits increasing slightly year by year, gradually accumulating. My uncle was also very frugal, and very trustworthy. He also opened a fabric and foreign goods shop, which was also quite successful. Unfortunately, in recent years, the market in that area has become increasingly depressed, and the area has been unstable, with frequent disturbances. We have been robbed seven or eight times, losing all our money and goods. Seeing this situation, my uncle knew that the situation was hopeless and that the end was near. He became ill with worry and eventually passed away. At that time, as a nephew, I was only thinking about survival, but neither was a good solution. During that time, I also studied at school for a few years. But the family was completely ruined. There was nothing for the old and young to do, and we had no cheerful relatives or friends. It was difficult for the eight of us to maintain our clothing and food, and I could not earn a single penny. Later, I was introduced by a relative, Deng Shaodun, to apprentice at the Huida Rice Shop in Wucheng. I was fortunate to have many teachers and friends who taught me earnestly, but I was inattentive and forgetful. Now, the shop's business has also ceased. My future livelihood is in great danger. In this situation, there is no joy in life, and there is great panic about the family's finances. Please, sir, give me the clearest possible direction. Answer: You are in Jiangxi, where the countryside is widely devastated, and it is difficult to maintain a livelihood. We are thousands of miles away. How can we give you a "clearest possible direction" out of thin air? This is really an impossible thing. Thank you for your letter from afar, asking so earnestly. We are sorry that we are unable to help! In the near future, this newspaper plans to select experts to go to Jiangxi and Hubei provinces to investigate the countryside. If this trip yields real materials, it may be of some help in the future for the reconstruction of your province and the provinces of Hunan and Anhui. This is also our way of repaying you.

High School Students Who Fail Three Subjects in the Joint Entrance Exam Must Take Remedial Classes 180

The Ministry of Education recently approved a directive to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau stating that high school students who fail three subjects in the joint entrance exam must take remedial classes according to regulations and will not be allowed to advance to the next grade. Junior high school students who take the exam with equivalent academic ability will be allowed to advance to the next grade, but will not be allowed to advance with graduation qualifications.

Nanjing Middle School Joint Entrance Exam Offers Preferential Treatment for Make-Up Exams 182

The capital's high school and junior high school graduation joint entrance exam, which began on the 22nd, has been going on for four days. The exam ended on the 26th.

▲ According to observations of the Chinese and English subjects already reviewed by the Social Bureau, most scores are above passing. In terms of schools, Jinghua Middle School and the Affiliated Middle School of Jinling University are the best. Although the remaining subjects have not been graded, the questions this time were all in line with the average level, and are not expected to be poor.

▲ Preferential Treatment for Make-Up Exams According to Lin Ang, the section chief in charge of the bureau, a small number of students have not taken several subjects. This would normally be considered as a waiver, but in order to protect the students' graduation prospects, they will be given preferential treatment. These students had previously requested the principals of their schools to ask the bureau for a special make-up exam. The bureau plans to convene the joint entrance exam committee after the exam to discuss the make-up exam procedures. Generally, the authorities of each school will be informed and asked to submit a list of students who have missed the exam to the bureau. At the same time, students who wish to take the make-up exam must personally come to the bureau to declare their intention to participate in order to show their seriousness. The date of the make-up exam will be within this week. The date of the second make-up exam for students who fail will be held in early next month after the elementary school make-up exam.

▲ Beginning of Grading All exam papers were sent by the chief examiners to the Social Bureau's supervisor, Zhu Wenbo, for safekeeping. The names on the exam papers were strictly sealed. The grading of the Chinese and English exam papers began the day before yesterday (26th). The French Municipal Council Promulgates Regulations for the Management of Schools 192

The French Concession Municipal Council recently promulgated regulations for the management of schools. Excerpts are as follows: Regulations for Application and Approval, Article 1: All institutions of a school nature shall be subject to the following special provisions. Article 2: Anyone who is approved to open a school shall report to the Bureau in accordance with Article 4 of the Branching Business Regulations. The report shall include the following documents: 1. A written report signed by the chairman of the school board, stating the nature of the planned school, the number of students to be enrolled, as well as the list of faculty members, school address, and budget; 2. A list of the names, addresses, and positions of each board member; 3. The principal's resume; 4. A drawing with a scale of 1:2000, indicating the location of the construction site adjacent to the school (surrounded by 100 meters); 5. Multiple drawings with a scale of 1:200, indicating the characteristics of the building and the internal layout of the school. This report shall be submitted to the Bureau at least three months before opening. Any reports that do not meet the above requirements will not be accepted. There are also provisions for hygiene and security, a total of Articles 3 to 12, as well as various regulations such as students suffering from infectious diseases and isolation rooms. The Chief Supervisor of the Health Department has the right to visit the school at any time to observe. However, for schools that have already been established, the Bureau may, when implementing these regulations, consider and handle them according to their actual existing status.

University Faculty Association Submits a Petition to the Ministry of Education Requesting Exemption from Restrictions on Enrollment in Arts and Law Faculties 193

▲ Lists Five Reasons for Consideration

▲ Please Obtain Unanimous National Opinion

▲ Then Determine the Highest Education Policy

The Shanghai University Faculty and Staff Federation held its tenth regular meeting at its headquarters yesterday afternoon at 4 pm. Zhang Shouyong, Kang Xuanyi, Lin Zhongke, Jiang Zhensan, Qiu Hanping, Zhang Jixin, and Chen Jiayi attended. Jiang Zhensan chaired the meeting, and Chen Jiayi recorded the minutes. The following motions were discussed: 1. The motion to send a telegram to the Ministry of Education suggesting that restrictions be placed on the enrollment of arts and law faculties in universities was passed as originally drafted. 2. The motion to organize a summer school to guide students in their studies was passed, and Kang Xuanyi was appointed to plan and implement it. 3. The motion on whether or not the Federation should take a vacation during the summer was passed in accordance with the decision of the eighth executive committee meeting to take a two-month vacation. If necessary, the documentation department will convene a meeting. The original text of the petition to the Ministry of Education is as follows:

Petition to the Ministry of Education 194

To the honorable Ministry of Education of the Nanjing National Government, we have recently read in the newspapers that the Ministry has proposed to restrict the enrollment of arts and law students in all public and private universities and independent colleges in the next academic year. The standard is that the number of arts and law students enrolled in each national and private university shall not exceed the original number of science students in that university. The number of arts and law students enrolled in independent colleges shall also not exceed the original number of students in that college in the 20th year of the Republic. After reading this, we believe that the Ministry intends to promote science education by restricting the enrollment of arts and law faculties. However, after repeated meetings and deliberations by our association, we feel that there are many difficulties in this plan, and it will not be easy to achieve the desired effect. We dare to offer our views for your consideration. 1. Our country has a long history and profound culture. Academic thought is extremely vast, and the social environment is extremely complex. Is it appropriate to focus solely on science education today and disregard arts and law faculties? This is still a major issue that has not yet been resolved. Germany's material science, mechanical engineering, and civilization are the best in the world, but we have not heard that this came from suppressing arts and law faculties. Furthermore, we have not heard that this has led to biased scientific

Abnormal Development 195

While legal studies has formed the continental legal system, and philosophy is a major center of the world. Previous examples are available and not difficult to learn from. Therefore, our association believes that it is best for the Ministry to carefully consider and deliberate on this matter, consult widely, and obtain the unanimous opinion of the national education community before issuing a final decision on the highest education policy. This is the first point to consider. 2. In recent years, our country has suffered from internal unrest and economic decline. National funding and private donations for science are very small. Therefore, public and private universities in our country are mostly incomplete in their science departments, and independent science colleges are even rarer. This is limited by reality and cannot be denied. If we follow the Ministry's new plan in the future, the basic teaching materials, library equipment, and domestic arts and law experts and professors of the original arts and law faculties will all be abandoned and left idle. On the one hand, science education will not advance because of the restrictions on arts and law faculties. On the other hand, private universities or colleges will not be able to continue to grow their existing achievements, and the new regulations for the future are not just empty talk. They will inevitably have difficulty surviving. This does not seem to be the Ministry's original intention of promoting education in a comprehensive and coordinated manner. This is the second point to consider. 3. Private universities across the country differ in their economic

Different Environments 196

Equipment has its pros and cons, and student enrollment varies. It is difficult to have uniform and predictable statistics on the number of students in a particular department in a particular school in a certain year. If we follow the Ministry's new order in the future, the schools with a particularly large number of students in the 20th year will still enjoy the great benefits of expanded enrollment, while the schools with a small number of students in the 20th year will suddenly suffer the strange disaster of permanent restrictions. There is nothing more unfair in principle and inconsistent in policies than this. This is the third point to consider. 4. Social undertakings in our country are underdeveloped, and the industrial foundation is extremely weak. This is because the people's living environment is difficult, the social economy is declining, and the government's promotion and protection of industry is misguided. Therefore, those who hold the country's power today and sincerely want to establish agricultural and industrial salvation policies, increase the efficiency of material science, should, on the one hand, widely provide national factories and reward private industries, and on the other hand, improve basic mechanical academics and popularize people's practical skills. The ratio statistics of industrial development and talent needs must be properly adjusted and planned. If we do not take this into account, and we see that today the nation's hundreds of industries are declining and industrial and commercial activities are failing, and large-scale factories and machine plants are as rare as morning stars, and the country is wasting national currency, and the graduates of industrial and commercial specialties at home and abroad who have already been trained still have no place to sell their talents and their studies are not used, and we do not consider the actual existence of places to receive them, but only seek to create a large number of high-achieving science students, it would be a waste of national financial resources and a waste of useful talent. Then, not only today's

Educational System 197

Is already chaotic, but the social impact in the future will only increase disputes, and it will be a loss in one fell swoop, and I have not seen its benefit. Critics say that today there is an oversupply of arts and law students, and they all tend to go into politics, which encourages the pursuit of fame and increases the atmosphere of frivolity. They do not realize that this is due to the disequilibrium of the nation's policies and the imperfect organization of the political system, which fails to make the best use of people's talents. It cannot be attributed solely to the large number of arts and law graduates. Moreover, if we consider the proportion of arts and law students in our country compared to the proportions in civilized countries in Europe and America, it is actually still insufficient. Even if we concede that there is temporary congestion in our country among those who study arts and law, they can still make a living by writing books. If science and engineering graduates are left over and society has no place to use them, individuals will feel the difficulty of making a living. If we look at the number of people who study science and engineering and become officials, there will be no shortage of them. This is not only a criticism of using what is not learned, but it will also cause people to study without being useful. It does not seem to be the intention of the Ministry to

Weigh the Pros and Cons 198

To achieve a comprehensive reform. This is the fourth point to consider. 5. Furthermore, our association has something it cannot refrain from saying. Today's social trends are becoming increasingly radical, and young people's minds are easily agitated. If the nation takes this as a hidden worry, it is important to have a good strategy for welcoming talent. If we do not do this and only restrict enrollment and suppress arts and law faculties, even if the country can reduce the enrollment, society cannot eliminate this kind of books, and the educational and academic systems will lose their guidance and scope due to the stagnation of arts and law faculties. Not only will there be few opportunities for students who aspire to this in the future, but it will also only make young people who are dissatisfied with the status quo more likely to resort to desperate measures. This does not seem to be the right path for the Ministry to rectify the academic atmosphere and reform education. This is the fifth point to consider. All these five concerns are inevitable consequences of the Ministry's new plan. Our association is worried and must report them. Therefore, we implore the Ministry to understand our concerns, withdraw the order, and discuss a new plan at length. The future of education will be fortunate, and the painful plea for life on behalf of our association will also be fortunate. Shanghai University Faculty and Staff Federation respectfully kowtows.

Opinions on Compiling Elementary School National Language Textbooks 199

The Municipal Education Bureau completed the compilation and submitted it to the Ministry of Education. The Ministry of Education issued a notice to the education authorities of various provinces and cities, soliciting opinions on the compilation of elementary school national language textbooks. After receiving the order, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau immediately convened researchers in elementary school education in the city to discuss the matter. As a result, each person submitted their opinions to the bureau for review. It is reported that the bureau has carefully reviewed and sorted out everyone's opinions on the compilation of national language textbooks, dividing them into ten categories: 1. Textbook content; 2. Text organization; 3. New words; 4. Font; 5. Word spacing; 6. Line spacing; 7. Textbook arrangement; 8. Illustrations; 9. Question practice; 10. Printing. They have submitted a small booklet detailing their opinions to the Ministry of Education for review.

The Ninth District Education Association Submits a Petition to the Education Bureau Requesting Equal Treatment for Teachers in Municipal Schools 201

Launched the Organization of a Teachers' Federation

(Guomin News Agency) The Ninth District Education Association, in response to the disparity in treatment between teachers in municipal, rural, and district elementary schools, has submitted a petition to the Municipal Education Bureau requesting that the treatment of teachers in municipal, rural, and district elementary schools be equal starting from the next academic year. The original petition is as follows: "Omitted above, the treatment standards for teachers in municipal elementary schools should be the same, regardless of whether they are in municipal, rural, or district schools. However, this is not the case. The salaries of teachers in municipal district elementary schools are one level higher than those in rural districts, and their annual seniority grade increases are based on the standard of one grade increase for every full year of service, and two grade increases for every three full years of service, and so on. However, the annual seniority grade increases for teachers in rural district municipal schools do not follow the standards issued by the bureau. They must have five full years of service to increase one grade, and ten full years of service to increase two grades. They are all municipal school teachers, but the treatment is very different, which is not fair in principle. It has been resolved by the general meeting to submit a petition to the Bureau for review and approval, starting from the next academic year, so that the treatment of teachers in municipal, rural, and district schools will be based on the standard annual seniority grade increase method, so as to achieve equality and fairness, omitted below."

It is also reported that the municipal school teachers in the district, in view of the organization of teachers' federations in municipal schools in the North and South cities, and the lack of contact between the municipal schools in the Ninth District, also believe that there is a need for organization. Teachers from Meilong, Longhua, Honglu, Zhangtang, Caonan, and Xinlong schools have launched an initiative and held a launch meeting at Longhua Elementary School at 2 pm yesterday. Wu Rugui, Tang Shugui, Zhu Yixing, Hu Wu峰, Zhao Jinwen, Chen Baozhao, Tan Chuanzhuo and other seven people were elected as preparatory members to be responsible for carrying out the work.

Essays

Mongolian Dictionary Publication Imminent 216

— Zhanlu

It is shameful to say that Mongolia is a part of our Republic of China; As for the "Mongolian Dictionary", I have never heard of anyone in the national writing community writing this groundbreaking masterpiece.

The Republic of China has been established for twenty-two years; People don't want to try to investigate and organize their own place, of course everything is isolated! Using the big to compare to the small, just like a family, holding five shares of property, at the very least, there should be five detailed and precise account books; if you don't set up account books, people will set up account books for you. Before September 18th, Manchuria was still our territory, and all the books and maps related to Manchuria's customs and products were written for us by Japanese writers as "ghostwriters" and "penmen". As a result, we gave away the property rights. The new term is called "non-resistance", and the old term is called "handing it over to others".

Manchuria is like this, and Mongolia is also a metaphor; many foreigners have set up account books for us; there is Schmidt's "Mongolian-German-Russian Dictionary" in 1839, Lavalevsky's "Mongolian-Russian-French Dictionary" in 1846, and Gorstinsky's "Manchu-Mongolian Dictionary" in 1895. In the mid-nineteenth century, many distant neighbors were already keeping accounts there; now, the Japanese writers' "Mongolian Dictionary", which took sixteen years of investigation and editing, will be published between this autumn and winter! The dwarves who are used to being "ghostwriters" or "penmen" are bothered, bothered.

It is said that this book is very rich, with tens of thousands of words, in addition to translating to Japanese, Chinese, Manchu, and Sanskrit are also included for comparison, and the price is about ninety Japanese gold. Although the price is expensive, after publication, there will definitely be a lot of Chinese people who want to buy it; The "dictionary source" of our territory does not need to be edited by ourselves, and we can feast our eyes for a hundred or so dollars. There is no need for officials; Chinese people are still officials, and Chinese people are really freehand friends.

Examination 217

— Yong Yu

A "ring" was set up on the Shandong Road, and a couplet of "punching heroes in the three mountains and kicking heroes in the four seas" was hung up. Countless "old monks" who "collect yin and supplement yang" from famous mountains and temples, "strange Taoists" who "spread beans into soldiers", and "black shop owners" who sell "human meat fillings" and "green forest heroes" who "knock people down with drugs" came to press down "life and death documents", jumped on the "plum blossom pile", and showed their faces.

This method of "comparing skills" is very in line with the principle of "survival of the fittest", and is called "natural selection". It is like the football match of "future Chinese masters" in modern "foreign schools". Only by "winning two out of three games" can they win the "big silver shield" back, and "take a day off to celebrate". Although "fighting on the ring" is "individual" and "playing football" is "group", "survival of the fittest" is "the same principle".

From "fighting on the ring" to "playing football", it is very logical to have a "graduation examination". That's right, how could "scholars", "juren", "jinshi", "hanlin", and even "Zhuangyuan and Di" not be "competing skills"? Only by comparing in this way can we find talents who can "govern the country and secure the people". You see, once the imperial examination system is abolished, the country will be so bad, so you know that only by "hard-hitting" comparison can there be reason.

This time, China is carrying out "graduation examinations" in a swift and decisive manner. This is a matter worth praising. It is said that this will enable the talents cultivated under the same system, like the "Big A Fu" made in Huiquan Mountain in Wuxi, to have the same face, one hundred or one thousand. A "Big A Fu" with a missing nose must be remade before it can be sold on the market. Students are also like this. If they fail in one subject, at the very least, they must endure their temper and condescend to be "old children" for another year.

It is said that this will not only make the students who don't study hard study hard, but also sweep away the accumulated malpractices of "requiring scope", "pass", and "cheat sheets". The students who participate in the "graduation examination" are like standing on the "plum blossom pile" to "compare skills". Those who have no skills don't want to stand firm. This is really the way to "select real talents". I don't know what the intention of those who oppose the "graduation examination" is.

Words After Heatstroke 218

— Rong Yu

The advent of all good fortune is like drinking ice cream. Is it just cooler in front of you, and not the same after drinking as before you drank it?

The kindness that a woman who sells everything gives you is like the wind from an electric fan. It's not real or natural at all.

The summer cicadas on the branches are like scholars who only sing high-pitched tunes. The more it knows and shouts, the more it doesn't know anything.

Summer is terrible, but not many people are sunburned to death by it. How cool is the night dew, but it kills tens of millions of people every year.

About Lan Caihe 219

— Huo Xueming

The commonly said Eight Immortals myth is uniformly said everywhere as: "Han Zhongli, Zhang Guolao, Han Xiangzi, Tie Guai Li, Cao Guojiu, Lu Dongbin, Lan Caihe and He Xiangu". As far as I know, all places uniformly acknowledge that only He Xiangu is a female immortal, and the rest are male.

Because Mr. Sun Liangong's Literary Dictionary said that Lan Caihe is also female, it caused a certain gentleman to refute (see the Free Talk in this newspaper on the 15th). He cited a song from Chen Tao's biography in Lu Fangweng's Southern Tang Dynasty, suspected that Lan Caihe may be Chen Tao, and determined that Lan Caihe is a male immortal. However, I know that before Lu Fangweng; regarding Lan Caihe's record, there is the Continued Biography of Immortals written by Shen Fen in the Five Dynasties, saying "Lan Caihe does not know where he is from, he often wears a tattered blue shirt, six knotted black wood belt, more than three inches wide, one foot wearing boots, one foot barefoot. In summer, he adds cotton to his shirt, and in winter, he lies in the snow, with steam coming out of his breath. He often sings in the city and begs, holding a large clapper, more than three feet long, often drunk and singing, old and young all compete to watch::: seemingly crazy not:::." In terms of time, of course the Continued Biography of Immortals is much earlier, so in this way, the Southern Tang Dynasty's so-called "There is an old man in Nanchang! It is suspected to be Chen Tao and his wife, clearly is a compilation, and is not enough to prove it.

Lan Caihe's song, in the Continued Biography of Immortals, is:

"Treading song, Lan Caihe! How much can the world do? Rosy faces are like spring trees, time flies like a shuttle, the ancients went on and on, today's people come more and more. Riding a horse in the morning, seeing the green fields turn into white waves in the evening. Long scenery and bright sunshine are in the sky, the silver palace is high and towering!"

So it is also very different from what is recorded in the Southern Tang Dynasty. There is also a "Buy Sorrow Collection" compiled by Qian Shanghao (Zhenzhi) in hand, and there is also a Lan Caihe entry, and the lyrics are not much different from the Continued Biography of Immortals, except that "to Biluo" is mistaken for "see Biluo" and "green fields" for "mulberry fields," and the last two sentences are missing.

However, in the fairy round scene of the Kunqu opera Dream of Handan, all the Eight Immortals are put in at once, ｜Although it does not match the plot of Li Mi's Pillow Book and Ma Zhiyuan's Dream of Yellow Millet｜The role of Lan Caihe is played by an old dan voice, which is like the Western opera supporting roles are mixed with high and middle tones as the standard; Mr. Liangong may have been fooled by the Kunqu opera book by recognizing Lan Caihe as a woman.

If you go to see the performance of Xian Yuan, you will see that Lan Caihe is wearing a scholar's hat, wearing a blue embroidered jacket, and is decorated as a gentle Confucian scholar. Lu Dongbin also sings, "Lan Caihe is a Da Yuan Ben Le Hu official!" Then, the question of whether Lan Caihe is "male or female" will not be as "indistinguishable as male or female" as Mulan.

Because I supplemented a certain gentleman's rebuttal, I wrote this article again, and presented it to Mr. Liangong.

▲ In a recent column, there was a eulogy about my late father that does not match the facts. First, my late father's body was strong and tall. A coffin was specially made after his death, so the burial was delayed for two days. Although we who are children cannot fully be filial, we also seek peace of mind, so even the clothes and coffins were very spacious, comfortable and strong, which resulted in a delay of two days. Secondly, the thunderstorm was on the 13th, and the burial was on the 14th. The weather was very clear, and the corpse must be swollen in the abdomen after being struck by lightning. This is common knowledge and is not worth being different about. Thirdly, the relatives and friends who sent the burial and the workers were all there, and there was no act of gouging the face. Fourthly, my family started at sea, and the East Gate is the ancestral hall. Shanghai has always been the hometown, and Jiayi is actually a villa. The person's hometown is untrue, and the other statements are even more difficult to prove. Fourthly, the ancestor was nearly one hundred years old when he was alive, and my late father was also nearly seventy years old. The reporter must be at least seventy or eighty years old, otherwise it would be fabricated hearsay. Only this section is not worth mentioning. Fifthly, my family's ancestral precepts forbid taking concubines, so my late father never officially took a mistress. However, in his later years, he was disheartened by national affairs and was not without indulgence. On that day, due to the large number of male and female disciples of my late father, some female students came to mourn, but there was no transmission of a conflict. Now I point it out, and I hope that the correction is grateful, Wang

Mengnian kowtows

Northeast Four Company Commanders 220

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Ten Hearing the Words Warns the Fragrant Heart, and the Hope of Conferring a Marquis is Vague.

Listening to the Song Shows Envy, and Repaying the Country Makes the Body Idle.

Guizhi knew that her mother was laughing for a reason, so she didn't ask too much. However, in some respects, the Zhao family's marriage seemed to be getting more and more real. If it continued in this attitude, the matter would naturally be successful. However, although Company Commander Zhao was a good person, she had never planned to have a military husband in her heart. Marrying a soldier was not her long-cherished wish. Thinking of this, she couldn't help but feel worried. She remembered that Liu Jiama on the west end of the street, her husband, was also a soldier. Why not take the opportunity to ask her what life is like as a soldier? At that time, she kept it in her heart and didn't say anything. Because she said to Jiang Shi, "Mom, you must have caught a cold. Lie down and rest for a while. Doesn't Liu Jiama have pills at home? I'll go get two to give you a sweat." Jiang Shi said, "No need, I can rest if I lie down for a while." Saying that, she lay down. Guizhi was a little worried that forcing her would arouse her mother's suspicion, so she didn't say anything that day. The next day, Jiang Shi was still tired. Guizhi said that she had to take some pills. After eating lunch, she walked to Liu Jiama's house by herself. They were also in the front and back courtyards. The front courtyard was a private school, where a Mr. Niu taught. Liu Jiama lived in the back courtyard with her son. Guizhi walked to the back courtyard, and Liu Jiama was washing cabbage leaves in the room. Seeing Guizhi, she pulled out two wet hands from the earthenware basin and smiled at her: "Rare guest, old girl, you have time to sit." Guizhi smiled and said, "No business, no visit to the Hall of Three Treasures, I have something small to ask you." Liu Jiama smiled and said, "Tell me. Pick what I can help with." Guizhi said, "My mom caught a cold yesterday." Liu Jiama said, "You want pills, I have, I have, I have. Come in, sit down for a while and then go, don't be in a hurry, it's warm in the inner room." Saying that, she lifted her apron, wiped her hands, and led Guizhi into the house. Guizhi said, "Liu Jiama, you are so frugal, you still keep the old cabbage leaves that you can't eat." Liu Jiama replied, "It's a pity to throw it away, grab a handful of salt and pickle it, and drink it with millet porridge, it's a good dish, if you don't believe me, try it." Saying that, she let Guizhi sit on the warm kang, took out a teapot from the kang eye, poured a cup of tea for her to drink. He smiled and said, "I can't even find a cigarette for you to smoke in a poor family." (One Hundred and Thirteen)

A Visit to the Film Studio 221

— Yi Zhou

One evening, I was huddled in a birdcage-like writing room, burying my head in writing work. Day after day, I felt like a writing machine.

Shanghai's most prosperous area is almost isolated from nature. When spring comes, you can't see any peach blossoms or willows, and you can't hear any swallows or orioles. When autumn comes, you can't see any yellow leaves or red maples, and you can't hear any cold cicadas or mournful geese. You just change your clothes as the air temperature rises and falls.

The early summer of "red cherries and green plantains" has unknowingly passed in a hurry, and the hot summer of "floating melons and sinking plums" is coming again, but I, who live in the prosperous area of Shanghai, am very isolated from these. I only see a few snack shops selling ice cream and soda, and foreign goods stores selling straw hats and fans, and I know that "summer" has passed by half.

In March, I planned to go to Longhua to see the peach blossoms, but I didn't go in the end. A few days ago, Mr. Feng and others initiated the Minhang summer tour, but I was tied up by things and couldn't get away. Yesterday, I was a little free and the weather was good, so I went to the Gujiatai Garden on Lafayette Road to get some fresh air, and on the way, I went to the Tianyi Company to visit the filming of the film.

Tianyi Company is located at the end of Ganshidong Road in the French Concession. The company is surrounded by a bit of rural flavor. To the south of the company, there is a large open space, planted with vegetables and the like, and there are more bamboo fences and tile houses. The owners inside are all farmers and workers in short clothes and bare feet. Being there is like being in the countryside.

In the summer of the year before last, when the company first opened the filming of silent films, I came to visit with my friend Mr. Xu, but at that time, because of other things, I just walked around in a hurry and left. This time, Mr. Shao Zuiweng personally received me, accompanied me to the photography site to watch the filming, and told me about the current situation of the company.

Outside the photography site, it was originally a wide square. Now it has been greatly transformed, with pavilions, ponds, flowers and trees, which is quite like a garden. In the northeast of the square, a small L-shaped pond has been dug. The pond is surrounded by green iron railings, and the banks of the pond are covered with green grass, interspersed with clusters of orange-yellow small flowers, which are very beautiful. A few small trees, a little taller than people, are full of green leaves. To the south of the pond, there is a hexagonal pavilion. The pillars and railings are all painted with vermilion paint, which contrasts with the green grass and trees, making it particularly beautiful. Outside the pavilion, there is a small plot planted with corn and cucumbers. The actor Wei Pengfei is adding fertilizer to the corn. Mr. Wei often plays a simple and honest old farmer on the screen. Now he is really doing farmer's work, which is really meaningful.

Walking into the photography site, I saw two sets built in the field, both simple and unpretentious country houses. Mr. Shao told me: the south side is the set of "Flying Catkins", and the north side is the set of "Struggle". At this time, filming had not yet started, and the field was full of people in short clothes and straw sandals. If their faces were not made up, they would almost be mistaken for odd job workers at the photography site. Yuan Meiyun was wearing a tattered dress with holes all over it. It is said that she plays a poor girl in "Flying Catkins", whose life revolves in a gray fate. Liu Binghua and Bao Zhichao have both shaved their heads. Mr. Liu is the male lead in "Struggle", and Mr. Bao is the male lead in "Flying Catkins". They are both young talents recently discovered by Tianyi.

The female lead of "Struggle", Chen Yumei, was sitting idly on the side because she had no scene. She was wearing a white sportswear and a sports cap on her head. It turned out that she had just finished playing basketball.

"Dangdangdang" A bell rang, which was a sign that filming was about to begin. Then the people in the whole field immediately became busy. Some were setting up the lights, some were arranging the equipment. Director Qiu Baxiang, with a script under his arm and a pencil in his right hand, would tell the actors how to perform, and then run to the camera to see the position of the lens, directing the cameraman to move the camera. Each shot took only two or three minutes of formal shooting time, while adjusting the light, aligning the lens, arranging the equipment, and rehearsing the actors took twenty or thirty minutes. I only watched them shoot three shots, and more than an hour had passed. Seeing that it was getting late, I said goodbye to Mr. Shao and went back.
